        <tr>
         <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style>
          <div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini">
           <ul>
            <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Administrative_levels_and_divisions_of_China_sidebar" title="Template:Administrative levels and divisions of China sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Administrative_levels_and_divisions_of_China_sidebar" title="Template talk:Administrative levels and divisions of China sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Administrative_levels_and_divisions_of_China_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
           </ul>
          </div></td>
        </tr>

      </table> 
      <p><b>Provincial-level administrative divisions</b> (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hans">省级行政区</span>; <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">traditional Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hant">省級行政區</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Shěng-jí xíngzhèng qū</span></i>) or <b>first-level administrative divisions</b> (simplified Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hans">一级行政区</span>; traditional Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hant">一級行政區</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">yī-jí xíngzhèng qū</span></i>), are the highest-level <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">Chinese</a> administrative divisions. There are 34 such divisions claimed by the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a>, classified as 23 <b>provinces</b> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">省</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">shěng</span></i>), four <a href="/wiki/Direct-administered_municipalities_of_China" title="Direct-administered municipalities of China">municipalities</a>, five <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_regions_of_China" title="Autonomous regions of China">autonomous regions</a>, and two <a href="/wiki/Special_administrative_regions_of_China" title="Special administrative regions of China">Special Administrative Regions</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">political status</a> of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Taiwan Province, People's Republic of China">Taiwan Province</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Fujian_Province,_Republic_of_China" title="Fujian Province, Republic of China">a small fraction of Fujian Province</a> remain in dispute, those are under separate rule by the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a>. </p>
      <p>Every province on <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a> (including the island province of Hainan) has a <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party of China</a> provincial committee (Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hans">省委</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">shěngwěi</span></i>), headed by a secretary (Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hans">书记</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">shūjì</span></i>). The <a href="/wiki/Party_Committee_Secretary" title="Party Committee Secretary">Committee Secretary</a> is effectively in charge of the province, rather than the governor (Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hans">省长/直辖市长/自治区长</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">shěng zhǎng/ zhí xiá shì zhǎng/ zì zhì qū zhǎng</span></i>) of the provincial government.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">
       <input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none">
       <div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr">
        <h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span>
       </div> 
       <ul> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Types_of_provincial-level_divisions"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Types of provincial-level divisions</span></a> 
         <ul> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Province"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Province</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Municipality"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Municipality</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Autonomous_region"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">Autonomous region</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Special_administrative_region_(SAR)"><span class="tocnumber">1.4</span> <span class="toctext">Special administrative region (SAR)</span></a></li> 
         </ul> </li> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#List_of_province-level_divisions"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">List of province-level divisions</span></a></li> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a> 
         <ul>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types_of_provincial-level_divisions">Types of provincial-level divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Types of provincial-level divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Province">Province</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Province">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The government of each standard province (Chinese: <span lang="zh">省</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">shěng</span></i>) is nominally led by a provincial committee, headed by a secretary. The committee secretary is first-in-charge of the province; second-in-command is the governor of the provincial government. In practice, day-to-day affairs are managed by a <a href="/wiki/Provincial_party_standing_committee" title="Provincial party standing committee">provincial party standing committee</a>, which makes decisions for a province analogous to the Politburo for the central government. </p>
      <p>The People's Republic of China (PRC) claims the island of Taiwan and its surrounding islets, including Penghu, as "<a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Taiwan Province, People's Republic of China">Taiwan Province</a>", though Taiwan has not been under control of a government that ruled from mainland China since 1949, when the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">Republic of China</a> (ROC) lost the mainland to the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party of China</a>, which established the PRC. (<a href="/wiki/Kinmen" title="Kinmen">Kinmen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Matsu_Islands" title="Matsu Islands">Matsu Islands</a> are claimed by the PRC as part of its Fujian Province. <a href="/wiki/Pratas_Island" title="Pratas Island">Pratas Island</a> and the Vereker Banks and <a href="/wiki/Itu_Aba" class="mw-redirect" title="Itu Aba">Itu Aba</a> (Taiping Island) are claimed by the PRC as part of Guangdong and Hainan provinces respectively.) The territory is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a> (ROC, commonly called "Taiwan") though the provinces were streamlined in 1998 and the provincial governments were de facto dissolved in 2019. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipality">Municipality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Municipality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Direct-administered_municipalities_of_China" title="Direct-administered municipalities of China">Direct-administered municipalities of China</a>
      </div> 
      <p>A municipality (simplified Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hans">直辖市</span>; traditional Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hant">直轄市</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">zhíxiáshì</span></i>; <small>lit.</small> 'direct-administrated city') or municipality directly under the administration of the central government is a higher level of city which is directly under the Chinese government, with status equal to that of the provinces. In practice, their political status is higher than that of common provinces. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomous_region">Autonomous region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Autonomous region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_regions_of_China" title="Autonomous regions of China">Autonomous regions of China</a>
      </div> 
      <p>An autonomous region (simplified Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hans">自治区</span>; traditional Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hant">自治區</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">zìzhìqū</span></i>) is a minority subject which has a higher population of a particular minority ethnic group along with its own local government, but an autonomous region theoretically has more legislative rights than in actual practice. The governor of each autonomous region is usually appointed from the respective minority ethnic group. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Special_administrative_region_.28SAR.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_administrative_region_(SAR)">Special administrative region (SAR)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Special administrative region (SAR)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Special_administrative_regions_of_China" title="Special administrative regions of China">Special administrative regions of China</a>
      </div> 
      <p>A special administrative region (SAR) (simplified Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hans">特别行政区</span>; traditional Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hant">特別行政區</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">tèbié xíngzhèngqū</span></i>) is a highly autonomous and self-governing sub national subject of the People's Republic of China that is directly under the Central People's Government. Each SAR has a chief executive as head of the region and head of government. The region's government is not fully independent, as foreign policy and military defence are the responsibility of the central government, according to the basic laws. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div>

It was streamlined in December 1998, with administrative functions transferred to the <a href="/wiki/National_Development_Council_(Taiwan)" title="National Development Council (Taiwan)">National Development Council</a> and other ministries of the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Yuan" title="Executive Yuan">Executive Yuan</a>.       <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_administrative_divisions_of_China" title="History of the administrative divisions of China">History of the administrative divisions of China</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sui_provinces">Sui provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Sui provinces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E9%9A%8B%E6%9C%9D%E8%A1%8C%E6%94%BF%E5%8D%80%E5%8A%83" class="extiw" title="zh:隋朝行政區劃">the Chinese Wikipedia article on the administrative divisions of the Sui dynasty</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sui_Dynasty.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Sui_Dynasty.png/300px-Sui_Dynasty.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Sui_Dynasty.png/450px-Sui_Dynasty.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Sui_Dynasty.png/600px-Sui_Dynasty.png 2x" data-file-width="1272" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sui_Dynasty.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sui provinces, ca. 610
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>By the time unity was finally reestablished by the <a href="/wiki/Sui_dynasty" title="Sui dynasty">Sui dynasty</a>, the provinces had been divided and redivided so many times by different governments that they were almost the same size as commanderies, rendering the two-tier system superfluous. As such, the Sui merged the two together. In English, this merged level is translated as "prefectures". In Chinese, the name changed between <i>zhou</i> and <i>jun</i> several times before being finally settled on <i>zhou</i>. Based on the apocryphal <a href="/wiki/Nine_Provinces_(China)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nine Provinces (China)">Nine Province</a> system, the Sui restored nine <i>zhou</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[9]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tang_provinces">Tang provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tang provinces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Tang_dynasty" title="Administrative divisions of the Tang dynasty">Administrative divisions of the Tang dynasty</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tang_circuits_660.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Tang_circuits_660.png/300px-Tang_circuits_660.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Tang_circuits_660.png/450px-Tang_circuits_660.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Tang_circuits_660.png/600px-Tang_circuits_660.png 2x" data-file-width="1319" data-file-height="931"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tang_circuits_660.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tang circuits, ca. 660
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:China,_742.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/China%2C_742.svg/300px-China%2C_742.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/China%2C_742.svg/450px-China%2C_742.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/China%2C_742.svg/600px-China%2C_742.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:China,_742.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tang circuits, ca. 742
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Emperor_Taizong_of_Tang" title="Emperor Taizong of Tang">Emperor Taizong</a> (r. 626–649) set up 10 "<a href="/wiki/Circuit_(political_division)" class="mw-redirect" title="Circuit (political division)">circuits</a>" (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%81%93" class="extiw" title="wikt:道">道</a></span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">dào</span></i>) in 627 as inspection areas for imperial commissioners monitoring the operation of prefectures, rather than a new primary level of administration. In 639, there were 10 circuits, 43 commanderies (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%83%BD" class="extiw" title="wikt:都">都</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%9D%A3" class="extiw" title="wikt:督">督</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%BA%9C" class="extiw" title="wikt:府">府</a></span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">dūdū fǔ</span></i>), and 358 prefectures (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B7%9E" class="extiw" title="wikt:州">州</a></span> and later <span lang="zh">府</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">fǔ</span></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETwitchett1979203,_205_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETwitchett1979203,_205-23">[10]</a></sup> In 733, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Xuanzong_of_Tang_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Emperor Xuanzong of Tang China">Emperor Xuanzong</a> expanded the number of circuits to 15 by establishing separate circuits for the areas around Chang'an and Luoyang, and by splitting the large Shannan and Jiangnan circuits into 2 and 3 new circuits respectively. He also established a system of permanent inspecting commissioners, though without executive powers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETwitchett1979404_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETwitchett1979404-24">[11]</a></sup> </p>

      <p>Other Tang-era circuits include the <a href="/wiki/West_Lingnan_Circuit" class="mw-redirect" title="West Lingnan Circuit">West Lingnan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wu%27an_Circuit" title="Wu'an Circuit">Wu'an</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Qinhua_circuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Qinhua circuit">Qinhua circuits</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Song_provinces">Song provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Song provinces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Northern_Song_Circuits.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Northern_Song_Circuits.png/300px-Northern_Song_Circuits.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="424" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Northern_Song_Circuits.png/450px-Northern_Song_Circuits.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Northern_Song_Circuits.png/600px-Northern_Song_Circuits.png 2x" data-file-width="796" data-file-height="1125"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Northern_Song_Circuits.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Song circuits, ca. 1111
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Song government abolished the previous commissioners and renamed their circuits (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%B7%AF" class="extiw" title="wikt:路">路</a></span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">lù</span></i>, literally meaning "roads", but however is still usually translated into English as "circuits"). They also added a number of "army" prefectures (<span lang="zh-Hant"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%BB%8D" class="extiw" title="wikt:軍">軍</a></span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">jūn</span></i>). Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Liao_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Liao Dynasty">Liao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jurchen_Jin" class="mw-redirect" title="Jurchen Jin">Jurchen Jin</a> dynasties also established circuits as the first-level administrative division. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yuan_provinces">Yuan provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Yuan provinces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Yuan_dynasty" title="Administrative divisions of the Yuan dynasty">Administrative divisions of the Yuan dynasty</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Yuan_Provinces.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Yuan_Provinces.png/300px-Yuan_Provinces.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Yuan_Provinces.png/450px-Yuan_Provinces.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Yuan_Provinces.png/600px-Yuan_Provinces.png 2x" data-file-width="1273" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Yuan_Provinces.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Yuan provinces, ca. 1330
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>China was reorganised into 11 provinces keeping most of the previous boundaries of provinces created by the previous dynasty unchanged, the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Yuan Dynasty">Yuan Dynasty</a> (1271–1368) had 2 addition regions: Central region ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Zhongshu_Sheng" title="Zhongshu Sheng">Zhongshu Sheng</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">中書省</span>) and the Tibetan region ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Buddhist_and_Tibetan_Affairs" title="Bureau of Buddhist and Tibetan Affairs">Bureau of Buddhist and Tibetan Affairs</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">宣政院</span>). </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ming_provinces">Ming provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ming provinces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ming_divisions.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Ming_divisions.png/300px-Ming_divisions.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Ming_divisions.png/450px-Ming_divisions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Ming_divisions.png/600px-Ming_divisions.png 2x" data-file-width="1275" data-file-height="902"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ming_divisions.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ming provinces, ca. 1409
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Ming Dynasty">Ming Dynasty</a> (1368–1644) kept the province system set up by the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Yuan Dynasty">Yuan Dynasty</a>, however, it divided the original 10 provinces into 16 provinces, later 2 capital metropolitan areas and 13 provinces (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">兩京十三省</span>) within <a href="/wiki/China_proper" title="China proper">China proper</a> and 5 additional military ruled regions. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Qing_provinces">Qing provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Qing provinces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_administrative_divisions_of_China_before_1912#Provinces_and_Feudatory_Regions_under_the_Qing_dynasty" title="History of the administrative divisions of China before 1912">History of the administrative divisions of China before 1912 §&nbsp;Provinces and Feudatory Regions under the Qing dynasty</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty_in_Inner_Asia" title="Qing dynasty in Inner Asia">Qing dynasty in Inner Asia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>By the latter half of the <a href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a> (1644–1912), there were 18 provinces, all of them in <a href="/wiki/China_proper" title="China proper">China proper</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">內地十八省</span>). Jiangsu and Anhui were originally one province called Jiangnan, with its capital at Nanjing. There was no discrete time period when the two halves of Jiangnan were split, but rather, this was a gradual process. </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r994648498">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
      <div class="div-col" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;"> 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Anhui" title="Anhui">Anhui</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">安徽省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">福建省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Gansu" title="Gansu">Gansu</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">甘肅省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">廣東省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Guangxi" title="Guangxi">Guangxi</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">廣西省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Guizhou" title="Guizhou">Guizhou</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">貴州省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">河南省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Hubei" title="Hubei">Hubei</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">湖北省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Hunan" title="Hunan">Hunan</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">湖南省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Jiangsu" title="Jiangsu">Jiangsu</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">江蘇省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Jiangxi" title="Jiangxi">Jiangxi</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">江西省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">陝西省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">Shandong</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">山東省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Shanxi" title="Shanxi">Shanxi</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">山西省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">四川省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Yunnan" title="Yunnan">Yunnan</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">雲南省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Zhejiang" title="Zhejiang">Zhejiang</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">浙江省</span>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Zhili_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhili Province">Zhili</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">直隸省</span>)</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_provinces">New provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: New provinces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">新疆省</span>) 1884–1912</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Liaoning" title="Liaoning">Fengtian</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">奉天省</span>) 1907–1912</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jilin" title="Jilin">Jilin</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">吉林省</span>) 1907–1912</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Heilongjiang" title="Heilongjiang">Heilongjiang</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">黑龍江省</span>) 1907–1912</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Taiwan Province, People's Republic of China">Taiwan</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">臺灣省</span>) 1885–1895</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Each province had a <i><a href="/wiki/Xunfu" class="mw-redirect" title="Xunfu">xunfu</a></i> (<span lang="zh-Hant">巡撫</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">xúnfǔ</span></i>; translated as "governor"), a political overseer on behalf of the emperor, and a <i><a href="/wiki/Tidu" class="mw-redirect" title="Tidu">tidu</a></i> (<span lang="zh-Hant">提督</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">tídū</span></i>; translated as "captain general"), a military governor. In addition, there was a <i><a href="/wiki/Zongdu" class="mw-redirect" title="Zongdu">zongdu</a></i> (<span lang="zh-Hant">總督</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">zǒngdū</span></i>), a general military inspector or <a href="/wiki/Governor_general" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor general">governor general</a>, for every two to three provinces. </p>
      <p>Outer regions of China (those beyond <a href="/wiki/China_proper" title="China proper">China proper</a>) were not divided into provinces. Military leaders or <a href="/wiki/General" class="mw-redirect" title="General">generals</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant">將軍</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">jiāngjūn</span></i>) oversaw <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a> (consisting of Fengtian (now <a href="/wiki/Liaoning" title="Liaoning">Liaoning</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jilin" title="Jilin">Jilin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heilongjiang" title="Heilongjiang">Heilongjiang</a>), <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, while vice-<i>dutong</i> (<span lang="zh-Hant">副都統</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">fù dūtǒng</span></i>) and civilian leaders headed the <a href="/wiki/Leagues_of_China" title="Leagues of China">leagues</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant">盟長</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">méng zhǎng</span></i>), a subdivision of <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Amban" title="Amban">ambans</a></i> (<span lang="zh-Hant">駐藏大臣</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">zhù cáng dàchén</span></i>) supervised the administration of <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>. </p>
      <p>In 1884 <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> became a province; in 1907 <a href="/wiki/Liaoning" title="Liaoning">Fengtian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jilin" title="Jilin">Jilin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Heilongjiang" title="Heilongjiang">Heilongjiang</a> were made provinces as well. <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> became a province in 1885, but China ceded Taiwan to <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> in 1895. As a result, there were 22 provinces in China (Outer China and <a href="/wiki/China_proper" title="China proper">China proper</a>) near the end of the <a href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span id="ROC_provinces_.281912.E2.80.931949.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="ROC_provinces_(1912–1949)">ROC provinces (1912–1949)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: ROC provinces (1912–1949)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">Republic of China</a>, established in 1912, set up four more provinces in <a href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia" title="Inner Mongolia">Inner Mongolia</a> and two provinces in historic <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>, bringing the total to 28. In 1931, <a href="/wiki/Ma_Zhongying" title="Ma Zhongying">Ma Zhongying</a> established <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hexi_Province&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hexi Province (page does not exist)">Hexi</a> in the northern parts of Gansu but the ROC never acknowledged the province. However, China lost four provinces with the establishment of the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Manchukuo" title="Manchukuo">Manchukuo</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a>. After the defeat of Japan in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> in 1945, China re-incorporated Manchuria as 10 provinces, and assumed control of Taiwan as a province. As a result, the Republic of China in 1946 had 35 provinces. Although the Republic of China now only controls one province (<a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province" title="Taiwan Province">Taiwan</a>), and some islands of a second province (<a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>), it continues to formally claim all 35 provinces (including those that no longer form part of the area of the People's Republic of China). </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r994648498">
      <div class="div-col" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;">

        <li><a href="/wiki/Zhili_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhili Province">Zhili</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">直隸省</span>) renamed <a href="/wiki/Hebei" title="Hebei">Hebei</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">河北省</span>)</li>

        <li><a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">河南省</span>)</li>

        <li><a href="/wiki/Hubei" title="Hubei">Hubei</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">湖北省</span>)</li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_province-level_divisions">Other province-level divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other province-level divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r994648498">
      <div class="div-col" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;"> 
       <ul>

        <li><a href="/wiki/Shenyang" title="Shenyang">Shenyang Yuan-controlled Municipality</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">瀋陽市</span>) 1947–1949</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin Yuan-controlled Municipality</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">天津市</span>) 1928–1949</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi'an">Xi'an Yuan-controlled Municipality</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">西安市</span>) 1948–1949</li>
       </ul> 
      </div>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Name</th> 
         <th>Hanzi</th> 
         <th><a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a></th>

         <th>Hanzi</th>

         <td><i lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language romanization">Xīzàng</i></td> 
         <td><span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">藏</span> <i lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language romanization">zàng</i></td>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Territories">Territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Name</th> 
         <th>Hanzi</th> 
         <th><a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a></th> 
         <th>Abbreviation</th> 
         <th>Capital</th> 
         <th>Hanzi</th> 
         <th>Note </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr bgcolor="#f5c3c4"> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Chamdo" title="Chamdo">Qamdo</a></td> 
         <td><span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">昌都</span></td> 
         <td><i lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language romanization">Chāngdū</i></td> 
         <td><span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">昌</span> <i lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language romanization">chāng</i></td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Qamdo" class="mw-redirect" title="Qamdo">Qamdo</a></td> 
         <td><span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">昌都</span></td> 
         <td>1965 merged into Tibet </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> abolished many of the provinces in the 1950s and converted a number of them into <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_regions_of_China" title="Autonomous regions of China">autonomous regions</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a> became a separate province in 1988, bringing the total number of provinces under PRC control to 22. </p>
      <p>In contrast, the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a> also had a number of provinces under its control such as <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province" title="Taiwan Province">Taiwan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fujian_Province,_Republic_of_China" title="Fujian Province, Republic of China">Fujian</a>, which the ROC currently administers, though the ROC abolished the <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_Province,_Republic_of_China" title="Xinjiang Province, Republic of China">Xinjiang Provincial Office</a> in 1992. In 1998, after streamlining of the two provinces, some of its powers from the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Provincial_Government" title="Taiwan Provincial Government">Taiwan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fujian_Provincial_Government" title="Fujian Provincial Government">Fujian Provincial Governments</a> were gradually transferred to <a href="/wiki/County_(Taiwan)" title="County (Taiwan)">county</a> governments. This fractured further between 2018 and 2019 when the ROC central government <i>de facto</i> abolished the provincial governments with most of the remaining powers given to the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Yuan" title="Executive Yuan">Executive Yuan</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span id=".22Lost_territories.22_of_China"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Lost_territories&quot;_of_China">"Lost territories" of China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: &quot;Lost territories&quot; of China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/20th_century" title="20th century">20th century</a>, China claimed that numerous neighbouring countries and regions in Asia were "lost territories" of China.<sup id="cite_ref-source_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-source-25">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Source2_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Source2-26">[13]</a></sup> Many of these "lost territories" were under the rule of Imperial Chinese dynasties or were <a href="/wiki/List_of_tributaries_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="List of tributaries of China">tributary states</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-source_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-source-25">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a> claimed that these territories were lost due to <a href="/wiki/Unequal_treaties" class="mw-redirect" title="Unequal treaties">unequal treaties</a>, forceful occupation and annexation, and foreign interference. <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a>, among others, were supportive of these claims.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[14]</a></sup> China published a series of maps during this time known as a "Map of National Shame" (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hans">国耻地图</span>; <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">traditional Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hant">國恥地圖</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Guóchǐ dìtú</span></i>) which showcased some of the "lost territories" that had links to various Imperial Chinese dynasties. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economies">Economies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The provinces in southeast coastal area of China – such as <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu" title="Jiangsu">Jiangsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang" title="Zhejiang">Zhejiang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> and (mainly) <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> – tend to be more <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialized</a>, with regions in the <a href="/wiki/Hinterland" title="Hinterland">hinterland</a> less <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">developed</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
